— Suo

People sacrifice their health, often simply due to a similar reason: they cannot manage themselves, leading to indulgence in life and excess in emotions.

Comic Strip

The Adventures of Sanmao the Soldier (108)

— By Zhang Leping

News Figure

Commoner President: Ju Zheng

— Qiao Zhi

"Short shirt and bare feet, holding a hoe and rake, trimming grass and watering flowers, leisurely and content."

"I was born late and suddenly reached old age, reading through the vicissitudes of life, the sea has become fields. I am ashamed to manage the state, but I fear to burn beans with the same root. The dream of Zhuangzi is confused by butterflies, and the wind and clouds of the Western Regions cry like cuckoos. I am happy that the autumn is high and people are healthy, unknowingly following the great way."

The above is a section from the "Poem on My Sixtieth Birthday" written by Mr. Ju Zheng, President of the Judicial Yuan, eleven years ago. Currently, the autumn weather is clear and refreshing, and our Mr. Ju is also getting healthier as he gets older. The content of the poem is very consistent with the current environment. Next month, the 20th, will be Mr. Ju's grand 70th birthday celebration. When toasting and writing poems, rereading old works will surely bring many reflections.

The President in a Bungalow

I call Mr. Ju a commoner president because, although he is the noble president, his private life is no different from that of ordinary people. Before the war, he built a residence near Hepingmen in the capital, occupying eleven mu of land. On such a large area, only a few low bungalows were built, which are truly as different as clouds and mud compared to the magnificent and tall Western-style houses of other dignitaries. At that time, the land and house prices totaled only seven thousand yuan. Every time the sun set, inside this house, there was often an old farmer in a short shirt and bare feet, wearing a straw hat, holding a hoe and rake, trimming grass and watering flowers, with a leisurely and content expression on his face. It may be hard to believe, but this old farmer was the dignified President Ju.

Mr. Ju not only likes the life of a farmer, but also considers himself an Australian. On June 14, 1936, he accompanied his wife to Shanghai and stayed at the New Asia Hotel. The registered name was a pseudonym, and the occupation column was filled with the two words "farmer."

Deeply Understands the Art of Living

He dislikes seeing strangers, but is happy to write calligraphy. Whether the person asking for his calligraphy is familiar or unfamiliar, he always responds. He loves to learn horse riding, and his favorite food is tofu.

Mr. Ju is from Guangji, Hubei, with the courtesy name Juesheng. He studied in Japan in his youth. Speaking of Japan, there is a nice story between Mr. Ju and her: when President Sun was running around overseas for the revolution, Mr. Ju followed and lived in Japan. For Mrs. Ju—Ms. Zhong—her compatriot—gave birth secretly, and Mr. Ju was burdened by having children while running around for national affairs. A Japanese friend, Kayanonagatomo, was willing to raise one of his daughters for him. From then on, Miss Ju was raised by a Japanese family and influenced by Japanese education. Twenty years passed in a flash. Mr. Ju was busy serving the country and forgot about this matter. It was not until June 1936 that Miss Ju learned about her background from her adoptive father, Kayanonagatomo, and then returned to China. The reunion of family members was truly indescribably bittersweet.

Mr. Ju currently has one son and three daughters. The eldest daughter is Kayanonagatomo, who lived in Japan in her early years and has married Mr. Zhang Ming. His son, Haoran, graduated from Tsinghua University and the Central Military Academy and is now serving in the military. He participated in front-line combat during the War of Resistance.

We want a commoner official, President Ju. The first impression people have of him is: "Living with the common people"; the "officials" we need in the future are also this kind of official. If we have a particularly good feeling for President Ju, the only reason is because "he is a commoner."
